# Python Data Analysis for Healthcare

> The healthcare industry is one of the most diverse sources of data, from clinical to administrative to sales and supply chain, and even regulatory data. This course with data scientist and pharmacist Wuraola Oyewusi teaches you how to use Python for a wide range of data analysis scenarios in healthcare. Wuraola covers practical use cases like statistical data analysis, data manipulation, wrangling

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare) | 2h 48m | Advanced | 19K learners
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

## Instructor

- [[Wuraola Oyewusi]]

### 1. Data Analysis for Healthcare

#### Data analysis in healthcare
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/data-analysis-in-healthcare?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/data-analysis-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=0)** - As training pharmacist, one of our deliverables was medication stock taking for tracking and forecasting.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/data-analysis-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=8)** This was one of my first exposure to medication data analysis.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/data-analysis-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=13)** Data analysis is applicable across industries.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/data-analysis-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=16)** Let's spotlight what it means in healthcare.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/data-analysis-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=20)** Data analysis.n healthcare is the process of collecting, cleaning, transforming, and analyzing healthcare related data to extract meaningful insight.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/data-analysis-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=32)** It is the systematic examination of the range of healthcare related data to find patterns and inform decisions.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/data-analysis-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=40)** Applied data analysis is a big topic in healthcare because of the availability of clinical and non-clinical data, and this means data backed improvement of both clinical and non-clinical outcomes.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/data-analysis-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=56)** Data analysis also enables resource optimization, which is a priority in the healthcare industry, and then every system that generates a lot of data benefits from the patterns identified either as pre or post-analysis.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/data-analysis-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=73)** Now that we've laid the foundation on how to think about data analysis in healthcare, we look at the types of data you may encounter.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/data-analysis-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=82)** Stay with me because we're getting to using Python to analyze healthcare a little later in this course.

#### Types of data in healthcare
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] When analyzing healthcare data, there are several common data types you would encounter.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=6)** Let's take a look at those now.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=9)** Categorical data.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=10)** This type of data is either here or there.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=14)** No in between.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=16)** Examples are medication names and specific diagnosis.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=21)** There is also continuous data.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=23)** Typically, numbers that can fall within a range, like vital signs and numeric laboratory values.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=31)** Ordinal data is a categorical data type that cares about other.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=36)** It is found in instances like patient recorded scores, like pain intensity.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=44)** For example, on a scale of zero to five, zero will be no pain, three will be moderate pain, and five will be severe pain.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=53)** An experience rating such as service rating.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=57)** Nominal data is typically numeric or alphanumeric that exists for naming purpose.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=63)** They are typically unique.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=65)** Patient registration number, for example, and maybe storage code for logistics and supply chain.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=72)** There is also time series data.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=75)** This is mostly longitudinal data.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=78)** Observations over a time of interest.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=83)** For example, hospital visit data over the years and disease tracking over a time range of interest.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=92)** We also have free text.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=94)** This is unstructured data.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=96)** It can either be hand written or digital.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=100)** For example, free text clinical notes and text service reviews.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=106)** You can also consider image data such as x-ray, radiographs, and other scans such as ultrasound, MRI, and CT scans.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=117)** And finally, there's genomics data related to genes.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=122)** Examples are DNA sequences and gene expressions.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=127)** We've talked about different types of data and we'll practice how to analyze these in a bit.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/types-of-data-in-healthcare?u=76281980&t=134)** But first, we'll look at where the data is coming from.

#### Sources of healthcare data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] We have established that the healthcare industry is broad.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=3)** Here are some sources of healthcare data and examples.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=7)** Clinical data that is directly related to treatments, electronic health records, or electronic medical records.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=15)** Laboratory and medical imaging data are examples of clinical data.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=21)** Administrative data.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=23)** This includes operational and logistics data, and then insurance, billing, and cost data.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=32)** In the digital age, patients also generate valuable healthcare data.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=37)** This includes data from wearables and health apps and also self-reported symptoms and online reviews.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=46)** We also have pharmaceutical data from manufacturing and drug development, and then from pre and post-marketing surveillance.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=56)** Data from public health and government.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=58)** Examples are disease surveillance and location data, like geolocation of public health facilities.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=67)** Research data.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=68)** This tends to be curated, and some are even published.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=72)** Examples are clinical trials, academic research outcomes, and curated research databases.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sources-of-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=81)** The sources mentioned here are by no means exhaustive, and you probably know many other sources of healthcare data from the work that you do.

#### Databases and storage for healthcare data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Generally, storage for healthcare data should be organized and secured like every other data type, and then extra security because of personal identifiable information.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=15)** They are stored in databases, which are software and on storage media, which are usually hardware or on cloud.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=24)** Databases are used to store and organize data in a structured and efficient way electronically in a computer system.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=33)** They are designed to manage, retrieve, and manipulate, and allow designated users to assess, update, and analyze information.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=45)** A database is not physical.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=47)** It's a software system.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=49)** A database ensures data structure and relationship, data integrity, data retrieval, security, and data scalability, backup, and recovery.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=64)** There are different types of databases.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=67)** The two major types are relational, which are structured tables with well-defined schema, examples of relational databases are MySQL, PostgreSQL, and Oracle Database, and NOSQL databases, which are flexible for structured and semi-structured data.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=90)** No defined schema.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=92)** Examples of NoSQL databases are MongoDB, Cassandra, and Redis.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=99)** And then we talked about storage media.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=101)** The types of storage media are hard disk drives, which are usually called HDDs, solid state drives, and then cloud storage.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=112)** The first two, HDD and SSD, are physical.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=117)** While cloud storage is accessed to a larger computer, typically over the internet.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=124)** This is the fundamental of healthcare data storage.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/databases-and-storage-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=127)** There are many variations, and there are many decisions that people make about how to study healthcare data, but behind them, foundationally, this is what the storage is about.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Env Vars:** nosql (1), hdd (1), ssd (1)
> **CLI Commands:** mysql (1), make (1)
> **Code Keywords:** type, (1)
> **Cross-References:** we talked about (1)
> **Speakers:** - [instructor] (1)

#### Data analysis tools and technologies for healthcare data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/data-analysis-tools-and-technologies-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/data-analysis-tools-and-technologies-for-healthcare-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] While this course is focused on Python for data analysis, data analysis can be done using a very wide range of tools and technology.
>

#### Correlation analysis of the patient visit demo dataset
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/correlation-analysis-of-the-patient-visit-demo-dataset?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/correlation-analysis-of-the-patient-visit-demo-dataset?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Presenter] Correlation is an interesting way to study the interdependence of variables.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/correlation-analysis-of-the-patient-visit-demo-dataset?u=76281980&t=6)** Let's visualize the correlation patterns in the numeric columns of the hospital visit dataset that we have been analyzing.
>

> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sentiment-analysis-of-patient-experience-reviews-using-textblob?u=76281980&t=159)** Polarity is the emotional tone of a message, and it ranges from a negative value of minus one to one, as the most emotional tone.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sentiment-analysis-of-patient-experience-reviews-using-textblob?u=76281980&t=169)** And then we have subjectivity.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sentiment-analysis-of-patient-experience-reviews-using-textblob?u=76281980&t=172)** If something is factual, it's zero.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sentiment-analysis-of-patient-experience-reviews-using-textblob?u=76281980&t=175)** If it's opinionated, it's one.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sentiment-analysis-of-patient-experience-reviews-using-textblob?u=76281980&t=179)** So, according to TextBlob, this sentiment is positive, this is 0.58.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sentiment-analysis-of-patient-experience-reviews-using-textblob?u=76281980&t=185)** So now that we know how this works, let's create a column called df_experience['Polarity'].
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sentiment-analysis-of-patient-experience-reviews-using-textblob?u=76281980&t=199)** We're going to apply to the entire column over the review.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sentiment-analysis-of-patient-experience-reviews-using-textblob?u=76281980&t=204)** So let's do df_experience['Review'] in square brackets, .apply(lambda x : TextBlob(x).polarity).
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sentiment-analysis-of-patient-experience-reviews-using-textblob?u=76281980&t=226)** If this goes well, when the data frame shows, there's going to be an extra column that has the polarity score for each of the reviews in the data frame.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/sentiment-analysis-of-patient-experience-reviews-using-textblob?u=76281980&t=240)** Yes, now we have a polarity column for each of the reviews.
>

#### Explore the public health facilities geolocation demo dataset using GeoPandas: Part 2
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/explore-the-public-health-facilities-geolocation-demo-dataset-using-geopandas-part-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/explore-the-public-health-facilities-geolocation-demo-dataset-using-geopandas-part-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In the last video, we began visualizing geopoints.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/explore-the-public-health-facilities-geolocation-demo-dataset-using-geopandas-part-2?u=76281980&t=4)** Now we will discuss buffers.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/explore-the-public-health-facilities-geolocation-demo-dataset-using-geopandas-part-2?u=76281980&t=8)** Buffers lets you create a sort of bubble between geopoints for better delineation.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/python-data-analysis-for-healthcare/explore-the-public-health-facilities-geolocation-demo-dataset-using-geopandas-part-2?u=76281980&t=14)** We will create the variable called buffers on the copy of the GDF DataFrame.
